<div id="review_1747659473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747659473" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1747659473?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747659473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer768046115026554998"><i>Lords and Ladies</i> is the fourth book in the <i>Witches</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. I enjoyed it, but not as much as the previous two <i>Witches</i> books. I thought the humor, while present, wasn’t nearly as strong as it was in the last two.<br/><br/>I think the humor seemed weaker because our main characters (Granny Weatherwax, Nanny Ogg, and Magrat, of course!) were often off doing separate things, and a big part of what makes me laugh in these books comes from dialogue between Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg. On the </span>
  <span id="freeText768046115026554998" style="display:none"><i>Lords and Ladies</i> is the fourth book in the <i>Witches</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. I enjoyed it, but not as much as the previous two <i>Witches</i> books. I thought the humor, while present, wasn’t nearly as strong as it was in the last two.<br /><br />I think the humor seemed weaker because our main characters (Granny Weatherwax, Nanny Ogg, and Magrat, of course!) were often off doing separate things, and a big part of what makes me laugh in these books comes from dialogue between Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg. On the other hand, Magrat actually had some decent moments in this book, although I expect she’ll continue to annoy me more often than not in future books.<br /><br />The story was pretty interesting, though, and I thought it was one of the stronger stories I’ve read so far in the <i>Discworld</i> series. To clarify, I don’t really consider any of the <i>Discworld</i> stories to be that strong so I’m not saying this is a story that will keep people on the edge of their seats, but it did hold my interest. I’m not sure how to describe what this one is about without spoiling the not-entirely-unexpected-but-still-interesting reveal about who the antagonists are, so I’ll just be vague and say that some wannabe young witches meddle with things they don’t understand and help certain unexpectedly evil and malicious beings gain a foothold into the world.<br /><br />I'm giving this book 3.5 stars on BookLikes, but I didn't enjoy it enough to round up to 4 stars here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="768046115026554998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16852313308838208848">[First read: 19th August, 2011: 5 stars.<br/>Second read: 25th July, 2013: 5 stars.]<br/><br/>Pratchett has an unbelievable knack for taking an idea that has been around for centuries, stretching it out with a rolling-pin and kneading it into something majestic and full of such originality you wonder how any could have missed it beforehand.<br/><br/>Those Witches are at it again. Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg are back from travels to fight against the Lords and Ladies--Elegant folk, fair, beautiful... glamourous.<br/>In te</span>
  <span id="freeText16852313308838208848" style="display:none">[First read: 19th August, 2011: 5 stars.<br />Second read: 25th July, 2013: 5 stars.]<br /><br />Pratchett has an unbelievable knack for taking an idea that has been around for centuries, stretching it out with a rolling-pin and kneading it into something majestic and full of such originality you wonder how any could have missed it beforehand.<br /><br />Those Witches are at it again. Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg are back from travels to fight against the Lords and Ladies--Elegant folk, fair, beautiful... glamourous.<br />In terms of humour, it's up there with the best of the funny Discworld novels. There are footnotes galore and you really can't get by without wiping laughter tears from your eyes at the sublime and the just plain silly. <div id="review_49031392" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49031392" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163750-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189653481p2/163750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49031392?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/163750-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">julia Andersen</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=fantasy-adult">fantasy-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=shakespearean">shakespearean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=fierce-females">fierce-females</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49031392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1240975904031821060">A fun twist on the basic ideas found in <i>A Midsummer Night's Dream</i>. Granny Weatherwax was especially awesome in this one; she is such a wonderful character. Magrat did some surprising things, too.<br/>I just have a little quibble about Pratchett's writing style--at times it can be like reading a play without enough attributions, the way he will set dialogue aside instead of attaching the action that goes with it. But his humour and other cleverness overcome that little distraction.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_49031392'><a id="like_count_review_49031392" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/49031392?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F34529.Lords_and_Ladies">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_810684024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810684024" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27302193-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513226227p2/27302193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/810684024?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/27302193-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27302193-james?shelf=james">james</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27302193-james?shelf=pratchett">pratchett</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer810684024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8074757137154357130">Another Discworld re-read, and another uptick in my original rating. I think that as much as I enjoyed and learned from Terry Pratchett when I was younger, there's something about reading this series in my late 30s that brings an entirely different perspective to it and appreciation for/understanding of the characters and the choices that they make. I genuinely believe that Granny Weatherwax is one of the best characters in literature. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EPxVtwfu2S028wwOOgo9E36FqIXq1pW96ikxjkb75skqGEAblA58eLnooBKidjjLXozL55dZpE0SRuBJHn4dpw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H4cceG9kYN1T0Y7BuFtobCQbcgQ/YffFK1SNAX4EV+4lYwnU/ITFiNzKIt0gJ220BBIRZkLuxjXTO1zGJoGsgA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5116974699313743884">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText5116974699313743884" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5116974699313743884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
